[HUMAN]: donald trump news

[AI]: Here's a summary of recent news regarding Donald Trump as of June 20, 2025:

**International Relations & Military Action:**

President Trump is currently weighing potential US action in the ongoing conflict between Israel and Iran and is expected to make a decision within two weeks, citing "a substantial chance of negotiations" (Al Jazeera, Anadolu Ajansı, The Hindu, DW). He has hinted at potentially joining Israel's strikes on Iran's nuclear sites (Al Jazeera). While his administration prefers a diplomatic solution, Trump has also signaled support for Israel's military campaign (Al Jazeera, Anadolu Ajansı). Russia has warned the U.S. against military intervention, while China has offered to mediate talks (The Hindu, FOX News). On June 13, 2025, Trump spoke with the UK Prime Minister about the Middle East, agreeing on the importance of diplomacy (GOV.UK). Trump is scheduled to attend the NATO summit in The Hague from June 24-25 (Hindustan Times, FOX News). He attended the G7 summit in Canada from June 15-17, holding bilateral meetings and signing an executive order to implement the UK–US Trade Deal (Wikipedia). He unexpectedly returned to Washington early due to the Middle East conflict (Wikipedia).

Regarding diplomatic efforts related to the Iran-Israel conflict, President Trump will decide within two weeks whether the US will join Israel's campaign against Iran's military and nuclear program, seeing a "substantial chance of negotiations" (Al Jazeera, AP News, Times of India). US Special Envoy Steve Witkoff has been in contact with Iranian Foreign Affairs Minister Abbas Araghchi, who has shown interest in resuming negotiations (Institute for the Study of War). Oman has been mediating between Iran and the United States (Institute for the Study of War). The US is working with European allies to de-escalate the conflict (AP News). British Foreign Secretary David Lammy stated that a "window now exists within the next two weeks to achieve a diplomatic solution" (AP News, Times of India, The Hindu). Some reports suggest Iran and its proxies believe that the United States approves Israeli actions in the region (Institute for the Study of War).

Key sticking points in negotiations include Iranian preconditions that there will be no negotiations while Israel continues its attacks (The Hindu, DW). The US insists that Iran give up uranium enrichment, while Iran refuses (Institute for the Study of War, YouTube). The US demands Iran dismantle all of its nuclear sites (Atlantic Council). The US and Israel share the goal of preventing Iran from having a nuclear weapon (Atlantic Council). Negotiations faltered after a round of talks in Oman were canceled due to Israel's aerial campaign against Iranian nuclear facilities (Times of Israel).

**Domestic Policy & Actions:**

As of June 17, 2025, Trump had signed 164 executive orders, 44 memoranda, and 70 proclamations (Ballotpedia). Recent executive orders include actions on the United Kingdom Economic Prosperity Deal (June 16), the proposed acquisition of United States Steel Corporation by Nippon Steel Corporation (June 13), and wildfire prevention (June 12) (Ballotpedia). A large military parade was organized in Washington D.C. on June 14 (Hindustan Times). Trump has directed ICE officers to carry out a mass deportation operation, leading to anti-ICE riots in Los Angeles, Seattle, and San Francisco, resulting in the deployment of the National Guard and Marines on June 7 (FOX News). He extended the TikTok enforcement deadline by 90 days to Sept. 17 (Anadolu Ajansı, The Hindu). Trump signed a proclamation restricting entry of foreign nationals to protect the U.S. from foreign terrorists and other national security threats (The White House).

The legal justification for the proclamation restricting entry of foreign nationals is primarily Section 212(f) of the Immigration and Nationality Act (INA), 8 U.S.C. § 1182(f), which grants the President broad authority to suspend or impose restrictions on the entry of any class of aliens whenever the President finds that their entry "would be detrimental to the interests of the United States" (Congress, NAFSA). The proclamation also cites INA Section 215(a) (8 U.S.C. §1185(a)) and 3 U.S.C. §301 (Congress). The restrictions, which took effect on June 9, 2025, involve a "full suspension" of entry for nationals from Afghanistan, Burma, Chad, Republic of the Congo, Equatorial Guinea, Eritrea, Haiti, Iran, Libya, Somalia, Sudan, and Yemen (White House, Congress, American Immigration Council, Al Jazeera, Gunster, NAFSA). A "partial suspension" of entry, with restrictions on immigrant visas and certain non-immigrant visas (B-1, B-2, B-1/B-2, F, M, and J visas), applies to nationals of Burundi, Cuba, Laos, Sierra Leone, Togo, Turkmenistan, and Venezuela (American Immigration Council, NAFSA, Al Jazeera, White House, Akingump). Exceptions exist for lawful permanent residents, existing visa holders, certain visa categories, dual nationals traveling on a passport from a non-restricted country, and individuals whose entry serves U.S. national interests (American Immigration Council, Akingump, Al Jazeera, White House, NAFSA).

Regarding the UK-US trade deal, on May 8, 2025, the United Kingdom and the United States announced a limited trade agreement referred to as an "Economic Prosperity Deal" (EPD) (Parliament, Dentons, World Trade Law, Two Birds). This deal aims to roll back some of the tariffs imposed by the Trump administration in March and April 2025 (Dentons). President Trump signed an Executive Order implementing American commitments under the General Terms of the United States-United Kingdom Economic Prosperity Deal. The deal is not a legally binding agreement but sets a non-binding framework for future bilateral trade talks (Two Birds, Dentons).

Key provisions and tariff reductions include:

*   **Automotive Sector:** Tariffs on UK cars imported into the U.S. will decrease from 27.5% to 10%, subject to an annual quota of 100,000 cars (Dentons, Sky, Woodland Group, World Trade Law, Brookings, Forvis Mazars, White House). Cars exceeding the quota will be subject to a 25% tariff (Forvis Mazars, Supply Chain Dive, Woodland Group). Tariffs on UK auto parts used in UK vehicles will also be lowered from 25% to 10% (Parliament, Forvis Mazars, Supply Chain Dive).
*   **Aerospace:** The U.S. has committed to removing tariffs on UK aerospace goods, such as engines and aircraft parts, which were previously at 10% (Sky).
*   **Steel and Aluminum:** The U.S. has agreed to remove the 25% tariff imposed on UK steel and aluminum (Dentons, Parliament, Al Jazeera, Sky, Woodland Group). The UK will be exempt from the global 50% tariff on steel and aluminum, remaining at the original level of 25% (Trade and Business). The U.S. intends to construct a quota at most-favored-nation rates for steel and aluminum articles, contingent on the UK meeting certain supply chain security standards (Sky, Dentons, Two Birds, Forvis Mazars, Parliament). The UK government has stated that the 25% tariff has been negotiated down to zero (Dentons, Sky).
*   **Agriculture:** The UK and U.S. have agreed to reciprocal market access for beef (Dentons, White House, Trade and Business). A tariff-free quota of 13,000 metric tonnes of UK beef can be imported into the U.S (Trade and Business, Dentons, World Trade Law). The UK will remove its 20% tariff on U.S. beef (Dentons, Trade and Business, World Trade Law). Tariffs on UK imports of ethanol from the U.S. will be reduced to zero (Dentons).
*   **Pharmaceuticals:** The U.S. and UK will negotiate preferential treatment outcomes for UK pharmaceuticals and pharmaceutical ingredients, contingent on the findings of a Section 232 investigation (Parliament, White House, Two Birds).

Impacted sectors include automotive, aerospace, steel and aluminum, agriculture, and pharmaceuticals (Forvis Mazars, Parliament, Dentons, Woodland Group, Sky, Supply Chain Dive, World Trade Law, Spectator, WeForum, Two Birds, White House).

**Other News:**

Trump's approval rating has fallen, matching second-term lows, with 41% of Americans approving of his job performance and 54% disapproving, according to a June 13-16, 2025 Economist/YouGov poll (YouGov). Trump addressed the issue of wildfires, stating his administration is focused on forest management (YouTube).

[parliament](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/2-0) [weforum](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/2-16) [woodlandgroup](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/2-10) [www](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/2-13) [dentons](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/2-1) [sky](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/2-6) [www](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/2-12)
*   **Agriculture:** Increased market access for U.S. agricultural products, including beef and ethanol, in the UK. [woodlandgroup](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/2-10) [twobirds](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/2-3) [whitehouse](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/2-9) [whitehouse](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/2-11) [worldtradelaw](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/2-2) [dentons](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/2-1)
*   **Pharmaceuticals:** Potential for preferential tariff treatment for British pharmaceuticals. [forvismazars](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/2-8) [whitehouse](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/2-11) [parliament](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/2-0) [www](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/2-13)

**Other Key Points:**

*   The UK will reduce or eliminate numerous non-tariff barriers that unfairly discriminate against American products. [whitehouse](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/2-9) [whitehouse](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/2-11)
*   The deal includes billions of dollars of increased market access for American exports, especially for beef, ethanol, and certain other American agricultural exports. [whitehouse](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/2-9) [whitehouse](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/2-11)
*   The UK is the only country to be exempt from the global tariff of 50% on steel and aluminum. [www](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/2-13)
*   The UK will maintain its food safety standards for any U.S. imports. [sky](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/2-6) [www](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/2-13)
*   The US maintains a baseline 10% tariff on most UK goods. [parliament](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/2-0) [aljazeera](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/2-5) [dentons](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/2-1) [woodlandgroup](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/2-10) [sky](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/2-6)
*   The agreement aims to streamline customs, secure critical supply chains, and set a precedent for future US trade agreements. [woodlandgroup](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/2-10)
*   The deal protects the UK from possible tariffs on semiconductors and pharmaceuticals. [parliament](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/2-0)

**Concerns and Ongoing Negotiations:**

*   The agreed tariff reductions on certain UK goods, such as steel and aluminum, are not yet in force. [parliament](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/2-0) [woodlandgroup](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/2-10)
*   Civil servants are still working on the deal, with disputes remaining over quotas on the amount of steel allowed before steeper tariffs apply. [spectator](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/2-15)
*   There are complications surrounding Chinese ownership of British steel. [spectator](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/2-15)
*   The deal does not address services trade, even though annual U.S.-U.K. services trade is substantial. [brookings](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/2-7)
*   The non-binding nature of the general terms generates uncertainty among businesses. [parliament](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/2-0)


--- Research Result 4 ---
The legal justification cited in the proclamation restricting the entry of foreign nationals, signed by President Donald Trump on June 4, 2025, is primarily Section 212(f) of the Immigration and Nationality Act (INA), 8 U.S.C. § 1182(f).  [congress](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-0) [congress](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-1) [nafsa](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-2)This section grants the President broad authority to suspend or impose restrictions on the entry of any class of aliens whenever the President finds that their entry "would be detrimental to the interests of the United States."  [congress](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-0) [congress](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-1) [nafsa](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-2)The proclamation also cites INA Section 215(a) (8 U.S.C. §1185(a)), which allows the President to prescribe limitations and exceptions on who may enter or depart the United States, and 3 U.S.C. §301, authorizing the President to delegate functions to executive branch agencies.

T [congress](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-0)he restrictions, which took effect on June 9, 2025, involve two categories of countries: those facing a "full suspension" of entry and those facing a "partial suspension."

Exceptions may also be made on a case-by-case basis by the Attorney General or the Secretary of State, in coordination with the Secretary of Homeland Security, if the travel advances a critical U.S. national interest.

The [whitehouse](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-4) restrictions apply to nationals of the listed countries who are outside the U.S. and do not have a valid visa as of June 9, 2025. The  [congress](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-0) [congress](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-1) [nafsa](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-2) [akingump](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-3)stated reasons for these restrictions include deficiencies in screening and vetting processes, high visa overstay rates, a lack of cooperation on accepting repatriated nationals, a lack of competent central authority, and/or a nexus to terrorism.

The proclamation also cites INA Section 215(a) (8 U.S.C. §1185(a)) and 3 U.S.C. §301 (Congress).
